WELL EVALUATION
Newfield Exploration
Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW
NWNW Sec. 22-T153N-R96W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
GENERAL:
On September 19, 2014, Newfield Production Company's Sand Creek Federal
153-96-21-28-13HLW was "spudded" as a Three Forks formation double section lateral
well. The subject well is being drilled in the Sand Creek field, located about 8 miles
north and 3 miles west of Keene, in McKenzie County, North Dakota. Keene is located
in the Central portion of the Williston Basin. Surface location of the Sand Creek Federal
153-96-21-28-13HLW is 33' FNL, 785' FWL, NWNW Section 22-T153N-R96W. Sand
Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW was planned with the ultimate goal of oil
production in the Three Forks formation. The horizontal well-path was planned to follow
structure with an estimated 89.3° average formation dip to total depth at 20,290' MD.
The well bore was planned to be drilled to the south following an azimuth along 184.38°.
OFFSET INFORMATION:
The main offset well for drilling Newfield Production Company's Sand Creek
Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW was provided from the Home Petroleum Federal 15-1.
The Home Petroleum Federal 15-1, API# 33-053-01203-0000, is located in Sec. 15 -
T153N-R96W.
ENGINEERING:
The Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW was drilled with Patterson-UTI
#344. Pad height of the Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW was 2171.3' above
mean sea level with the Kelly bushing located at 2,196.3' above mean sea level, 25'
above ground level.
The Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW was drilled with fresh water from
surface to 1,892' MD. A switch was then made, and oil base mud was used from 1,892'
MD to 10,694' MD. Once horizontal the OBM was replaced by brine and it was used
from 10,694' MD to TD at the end of the well at 20,300' MD (see mud report summary).
Initially, the Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW was drilled as a 13 1/2"
hole to 1,892' MD, and 9 5/8" 36# J-55 casing was set to a depth of 1,886' through the
Fox Hills formation. The Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW then progressed as
an 8 ¾" hole from the base of the Fox Hills formation until KOP. Kick off point was
reached in the base of the Lodgepole Formation on September 26, 2014 at a measured
depth of 9,820'. At KOP a trip was made to pick up a mud motor with a 2.2° fixed bend
and a new bit. Directional work from here was performed by Chijioke Onyekwere, Kyle
Blair, and Andrew Murphy from Baker Hughes directional services. The curve from
vertical to horizontal was then drilled starting from 9,820' MD and landing horizontal at
10,694' MD (10,335' TVD). The curve was drilled holding an average build rate of 10.5°
WELL EVALUATION
Newfield Exploration
Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW
NWNW Sec. 22-T153N-R96W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
and was landed on September 27, 2014. Once landed, 7" 29# HPL-80 intermediate
casing was set to a depth of 10,674', through the salts and curve to horizontal and then
cemented in place.
The main lateral of Newfield Production Company's Sand Creek Federal 153-96-
21-28-13HLW began on October 26, 2014. It was drilled from 10,694' MD to a TD at
20,300' MD. At td a 4 1/2" perforated liner was run through the lateral to a depth of
20,280' MD. Fracture stimulation is planned to enhance the well.
The Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW was completed with (6) six drill
bits, and took a total of 210.5 hours to complete, for an average penetration rate of 86.6
feet per hour (see attached bit record summary).
For the lateral the well bore was within the Three Forks formation for 100% of the
time, 63.4% in the primary Three Forks target, 6% above the primary Three Forks
target, and 30.6% below the primary Three Forks target. The well bore was within the
upper Three Forks "B" facies for 69.4% of the time, the upper Three Forks "A"facies for
23.5% of the time, and the middle Three Forks "C" facies for 7.1% of the time.
GEOLOGICAL EVALUATION:
Geologic supervision of the Newfield Production Company's Sand Creek Federal
153-96-21-28-13HLW well was provided by Geo-Link Geological Services with two-man
geo-steering and geological consulting service. Geologic evaluation began at a
measured depth of 8,500' in the Charles formation and continued until TD (20,300'MD)
at the end of the lateral. A MSI "blue box" and Pason total gas analyzer were used to
record gas levels at the rigs shakers during the vertical, curve, and lateral portions of
the well. The gas data was then integrated into the log along with drilling rate and also
gamma data provided by Baker Hughes directional services. Lagged samples for the
well were caught by the rig crews in 30' intervals from 8,500' until 10,670' and then 100'
intervals from 10,600' until total depth was reached at 20,300'. These cuttings were
examined under a binocular microscope, photographed, and placed under a UV
fluoroscope. Cuttings were tested with acid and Alizarin Red to distinguish between
carbonates. Naphthalene and Acetone were used to examine oil cut from the samples.
Sample descriptions and properties where then noted in the logs. After sample
evaluation, a set of dried cuttings were saved for the state of North Dakota.
As seen in the "Calculated Target" table, the target dropped 101.8' from a TVD of
10,341.2' at the start of the lateral at 10,540' MD to 10,443' TVD at the end of the lateral
at 20,300' MD at an average dip of 89.36 degrees on the Sand Creek Federal 153-96-
21-28-13HLW. It was a down dip for almost the entire lateral. The steepest down dip we
saw was 88.80 degrees.
Fair to occasional good oil shows were observed in dolomites of poor to
occasionally good visible intercrystalline porosity. The gas and oil shows observed
WELL EVALUATION
Newfield Exploration
Sand Creek Federal 153-96-21-28-13HLW
NWNW Sec. 22-T153N-R96W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
while drilling the Three Forks dolomites indicate that the Sand Creek Federal 153-96-
21-28-13HLW will be a commercially productive well.
Thank you for the opportunity to serve as Newfield Production Company's well site
geologists on this well. If you have any questions, please do not hesitate to contact me
or Geo-Link, Inc.

John Vogelzang, James Bennett II, Zach Fortney

Well File # 29268
Dear Karen:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24510, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is
granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, shall be located approximately down the
north-south axis (500' drilling corridor per Commission policy) and be no closer than the 200' setback from the north &
south boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 21, 22, 27, 28 T153N R96W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: IN CASES WHERE A SPACING UNIT IS ACCESSED FROM AN OFF-SITE
DRILL PAD, AN AFFIDAVIT MUST BE PROVIDED AFFIRMING THAT THE SURFACE OWNER OF
THE MULTI-WELL PAD AGREES TO ACCEPT BURIAL ON THEIR PROPERTY OF THE CUTTINGS
GENERATED FROM DRILLING THE WELL INTO THE SPACING UNIT. Effective June 1, 2014, a covered
leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the
well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire location.
NEWFIELD PRODUCTION COMPANY must ensure the drilling pit is not constructed in a porous material
(i.e.: sand, coal, gravel, or scoria). NEWFIELD PROD CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Samuel Skurupey
at 701-770-1981 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and
completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of
the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be
inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized
in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinates from the well head at casing point are: 167 S
& 535 W. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10315 S.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved
drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd
business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director.
Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating
circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that would allow the Director to
conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.

Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall
file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be
submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional
survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a
timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a certification cover page to
certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when
sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date the
well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records wherever
located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the Director and his
representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them, complying with all
safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to any and all records of
wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such
wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be
maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail
cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or
initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

hydrocarbons, fresh water zones, abnormal pressure zones,
and prospectively valuable mineral deposits.
A. Casing head: 9 5/8" SOW x 11" 5M multi-bowl w/ flange at ground level.Initial BOPE test to 5000 psi.

B. Operators minimum specifications for pressure control equipment are shown on the attached BOP
schematic.
After running surface casing and prior to drilling out, blind rams, pipe rams, manifold,
upper and lower kelly cock and safety valve will be pressure tested to 5000 psi. Hydril will be tested
to 2500 psi. Thereafter, the BOPE will be checked daily for mechanical operations and will be noted
in the IADC drilling reports. Before and after running the intermediate casing the BOPE will be tested
in the same manner. BOP will be tested at low pressure to 250 psi.
Gas Buster will be fully rigged up and tested for fluid integrity, using anti-freeze solution
prior to drilling out surface casing.

D. Other Drilling Considerations & Lessons Learned:
1. Gas Buster- Not to be used for venting off flowline. Divert all flow to gas buster.
2. Lateral Drilling- Minimize DLS.
3. Salt Sections: Tight hole and stuck pipe may occur. Control drill +/-5' and back-ream
as necessary. Spot freshwater only if severely stuck.
4. Do not rotate PDC bit inside 7" casing while displacing well with kill weight fluids.
Ensure bit & motor are in open hole section.
5. Transfer OBM from storage tanks to rig tanks over the shaker screens.
6. CaCL Brine truck to location after running/cmt'g 7 inch csg.

McKenzie County, North Dakota
To whom it may concern:
This notice is intended to confirm that the proposed completion consisting of hydraulic fracture treatment
on the above mentioned well is in compliance with EPA UIC Program Guidance #84 regarding oil and
gas hydraulic fracturing activities using diesel fuels. Newfield is aware of the EPA guidance and does
not intend to inject "diesel fuels" in any quantity. Newfield has confirmed with its fracturing service
provider that "diesel fuels" are not included in the chemicals injected during fracturing treatment of
Newfield operated wells. The above referenced "diesel fuels" are described below by Chemical Abstract
Service Registry Number (CASRN):
1) 68334-30-5 Primary Name: Fuels, diesel
2) 68476-34-6 Primary Name: Fuels, diesel, No. 2
3) 68476-30-2 Primary Name: Fuel oil No. 2
4) 68476-31-3 Primary Name: Fuel oil, No. 4
5) 8008-20-6 Primary Name: Kerosene

Subject: RE: Sand Creek Federal 15396212813HLW

Sara,

The Forest Service has received the APD and Surface Use Plan of Operations (SUPO) for the proposed Newfield Sand
Creek Federal 15396212813HLW located in the NWNW Section 22, T153N, R96W. This proposed well will be added
to the existing Helsingborg Federal 1539622272H, 3H, & 10H well pad with no further surface disturbance being
needed. We are currently working on completing the approval of this SUPO and at this time do not have any objections
to what is being proposed. Once we have approved the SUPO it will be sent back to the BLM for final approval of the
APD.

Please let me know if you have any other questions or need anything else from me at this time.
